<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scout_moor_gearbox,_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Scout_moor_gearbox%2C_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg/220px-Scout_moor_gearbox%2C_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Scout_moor_gearbox%2C_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg/330px-Scout_moor_gearbox%2C_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Scout_moor_gearbox%2C_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg/440px-Scout_moor_gearbox%2C_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scout_moor_gearbox,_rotor_shaft_and_brake_assembly.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Typical components of a wind turbine (gearbox, rotor shaft and brake assembly) being lifted into position</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">Wind turbines</a> are devices that convert the wind's <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">kinetic energy</a> into electrical power. The result of over a millennium of <a href="/wiki/Windmill" title="Windmill">windmill</a> development and modern engineering, today's wind turbines are manufactured in a wide range of horizontal axis and <a href="/wiki/Vertical_axis_wind_turbine" title="Vertical axis wind turbine">vertical axis</a> types. The smallest turbines are used for applications such as <a href="/wiki/Battery_charger" title="Battery charger">battery charging</a> for auxiliary power. Slightly larger turbines can be used for making small contributions to a domestic power supply while selling unused power back to the utility supplier via the <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">electrical grid</a>. Arrays of large turbines, known as <a href="/wiki/Wind_farm" title="Wind farm">wind farms</a>, have become an increasingly important source of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> and are used in many countries as part of a strategy to reduce their reliance on <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>.
</p><p>Wind turbine design is the process of defining the form and specifications of a <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">wind turbine</a> to extract energy from the <a href="/wiki/Wind" title="Wind">wind</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BERR_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-BERR-266">[264]</a></sup>
A wind turbine installation consists of the necessary systems needed to capture the wind's energy, point the turbine into the wind, convert <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_energy" title="Mechanical energy">mechanical rotation</a> into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrical_power" title="Electrical power">electrical power</a>, and other systems to start, stop, and control the turbine.
</p><p>In 1919 the German physicist <a href="/wiki/Albert_Betz" title="Albert Betz">Albert Betz</a> showed that for a hypothetical ideal wind-energy extraction machine, the fundamental laws of conservation of mass and energy allowed no more than 16/27 (59.3%) of the kinetic energy of the wind to be captured. This <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Betz%27_law" title="Betz' law">Betz limit</a> can be approached in modern turbine designs, which may reach 70 to 80% of the theoretical Betz limit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[265]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[266]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_aerodynamics" title="Wind turbine aerodynamics">aerodynamics of a wind turbine</a> are not straightforward. The air flow at the blades is not the same as the airflow far away from the turbine. The very nature of the way in which energy is extracted from the air also causes air to be deflected by the turbine. In addition the <a href="/wiki/Aerodynamics" title="Aerodynamics">aerodynamics</a> of a wind turbine at the rotor surface exhibit phenomena that are rarely seen in other aerodynamic fields. The shape and dimensions of the blades of the wind turbine are determined by the aerodynamic performance required to efficiently extract energy from the wind, and by the strength required to resist the forces on the blade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[267]</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to the aerodynamic <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Blade_design" title="Wind turbine design">design of the blades</a>, the design of a complete wind power system must also address the design of the installation's <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#The_hub" title="Wind turbine design">rotor hub</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nacelle_(wind_turbine)" title="Nacelle (wind turbine)">nacelle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine_design#Tower" title="Wind turbine design">tower structure</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_generator" title="Electric generator">generator</a>, controls, and foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-univ2011_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-univ2011-270">[268]</a></sup>
Turbine design makes extensive use of computer modelling and simulation tools. These are becoming increasingly sophisticated as highlighted by a recent state-of-the-art review by Hewitt et al.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hewitt2017_271-0"><a href="#cite_note-hewitt2017-271">[269]</a></sup> 
Further design factors must also be considered when integrating wind turbines into <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">electrical power grids</a>.
</p>

Archived from <a class="external text" href="http://www.nrel.gov/wind/systemsintegration/system_integration_basics.html" rel="nofollow">the original</a> on 7 June 2012.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Wind+Systems+Integration+Basics&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.nrel.gov%2Fwind%2Fsystemsintegration%2Fsystem_integration_basics.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AWind+power"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Diesendorf-132"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Diesendorf_132-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Diesendorf, Mark (2007). "<a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_Solutions_with_Sustainable_Energy" title="Greenhouse Solutions with Sustainable Energy">Greenhouse Solutions with Sustainable Energy</a>": 119. <q>Graham Sinden analysed over 30 years of hourly wind speed data from 66 sites spread out over the United Kingdom. He found that the correlation coefficient of wind power fell from 0.6 at 200 km to 0.25 at 600 km separation (a perfect correlation would have a coefficient equal to 1.) There were no hours in the data set where wind speed was below the cut-in wind speed of a modern wind turbine throughout the United Kingdom, and low wind speed events affecting more than 90 per cent of the United Kingdom had an average recurrent rate of only one hour per year.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=Greenhouse+Solutions+with+Sustainable+Energy&amp;rft.pages=119&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.au=Diesendorf%2C+Mark&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AWind+power"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>
</li>
